asked the Minister of Education :

(a) Will he inform this House separately—

(i) the number of computer operators serving in theOpen University of Sri Lanka; and

(ii) out of them, the number of casual employees whowork on piece rate?

(b) Will he state the obstacles to the absorption of thosecasual employees into the permanent service?

(c) Will he take action to place these casual employeesin the permanent service?

(d) If not why?

But what has happened? TheEDB is dead. Then if you take the IDB, the IDB was there tobasically do exactly what this Act is seeking to do. Remember that isthe strength we are extending as a party that has got 47 lakhsof votes. That is a commitment we have and that is the stylewe adopt in taking this country forward. We know things arehappening. We are there to ensure that we take the countryforward.

Then, Sir, look at the Free Trade Agreements, the IndianFree Trade Agreement the Hon. Jeyaraj Fernandopulle wastelling about the problems he has with India. I share his viewson the problems. I do not want to be mincing words becauseI know the problems he has. When you have Free Trade Agree-ments and there are people diametrically opposite trying tooppose that type of thing how can there be an Indian FreeTrade Agreement? Regarding the USE Free Trade Agree-ment, people said, We do not want the Free Trade Agreement.Now what are we going to do for the 66 per cent of textilesexported? Then the WTO, they made such a big noise. At themeeting we had in Cancun we placed Sri Lanka on the map.Back again they came and ridiculed us. At the end of the day

what happened? You went to Hong Kong on bended kneesand you went even further than we did. The world is chang-ing and that is why we say that you have to be in with this.

Then regarding the labour GSP, the hon. Prof. G. L. Peirisand I on the instructions of the Hon. Ranil Wickremasinghewent to Brussels and got the labour GSP. The benefits camein our administration but the final benefit came in your ad-ministration. But what has happened, Sir? Today you havethe labour GSP which at least has exports going to Europe ata concessionary duty entry. That is under threat.

I read your statement today and I am happy that once againthe UNP is awakened and has things to be done there-“Rohitha dismisses fears but Apparved industries worried.”Remember Ashroff Omar’s Brandix Apparel Limited,Amaleens’ apparel industries all are worried. What you say isnot what is happening. You by yourself cannot do this. Thatis why I say, do not let us lose this GSP opportunity.

Then you were also talking of borrowing Us Dollars 1000million in order to pay off the debts of this country. Today Ihave got a document that was tabled in Parliament by theHon. Minister of Finance which refers to the amortization ofthe year 2006 - that is capital repayment and the interestpayment which is rouhgly Rs. 455 billion. So, is it that thisGovernment is going to borrow US Dollars 1000 million inorder to pay this Rs. 455 billion and put the country into adebt trap? Please stop playing with the economy. This iswhat happened to Taiwan. This is what happened to Thai-land and this is what happened to Korea in 1996. You borrowmoney at 6 per cent whan your earnings are at 2 per cent andfall into a debt trap. We are warning you today. Please do notplay with the national economy of this country. The value ofthe US Dollar is sliding. Now it is Rs. 103. When we handedover the government it was Rs. 97. If you are unable to dealwith this type of national debts that are taken with foreignreserves increasing you will never be able to stop the Valueof the US Dollar even at Rs. 120. When that happens it is notthe Government but it is the entire country that has to pay forthis.

So, I am basically warning you from a national point ofview, from a country’s point of view and from the point ofview of the United National Party. We as responsible peoplehave feelings please do not let these things happen. If youare unable, say we cannot, yes, we duped the people. But donot play around with the economy. Let people shriek. Letthem stop at that. But ensure that the country goes forward.

Then, Sir, I come to an important statement which hadbeen referred to in the news papers, a statement that had beenmade in Parliament yesterday and basically a big noise hadbeen made by Mr. Wimal Weerawansa. I quote from the Agreement with Mr. Tylvin Silva. signed bythe then Prime Minister Mahinda Rajapaksa during the timehe was a presidential Candidate Sir, paragraph two of theAgreement says, I quote;

“2. We believe that it is necessary to have negotiations not only withthe LTTE but also with all other relevant parties to resolve Sri Lanka’snational question and that without being agreed on such lasting solutionit is agreed hereby not to grant Interim Self-governing Authority orany such political or administrative structure to LTTE or to holdnegotiations with LTTE on that basis.’’

Member will ask what relevancehas this got with national enterprise development. yes,national enterprise development is basically reducing cost.Reducing costs means having no war. I think the hon. Member Ravi Karunanayake, my goodFriend, has fast become the sole voice of the United NationalParty. I congratulate him on that. At the same time certainaspersions were cast on the peace initiative that has beentaken by His Excellency the President, during the speechmade by my good Friend.

If there are any questions that the hon. Member wishes usto respond to from the Government Benches I would like todo so in terms of the peace process keeping in line with theUnited National Party’s thinking on the matter.

Sir, I was a party to the All Party Conference that was heldon Monday of this week where the United National Party ledby its Deputy Leader, hon. Karu Jayasuriya endorsed the stepsthat have been taken by the President in initiating the peace

process. Also, all the parties joined in endorsing and acceptingthe formulas that we have been working on. So if there areany specific issues on which the hon. Member from the UNPbenches wishes the Government to respond, to in line withthe serious engagement now we have made to bring aboutlasting peace in the country, I would like the hon. Member tohave structured questions put across to us, so that we will beable to respond to from the point of view of the Government.

Then Sir, in relation to the three issues that were raised inline with what I have submitted in the National EnterpriseDevelopment Authority Bill about the BOI, the EDB and theIDB, I wish to state that they are distinct and seperateorganizations, institutions that are meant to service certainaspects of different areas other than that of the SME Authority.Thereby I think the hon. Member will be leared enough tounderstand the need for the SME Authority. These are theclarifications I wish to present. Thank you.

Hussein Ahamed Bhaila - Deputy Minister of PlanImplementation)Thank you, Mr. Deputy Speaker, for giving me thisopportunity to speak on this very important Bill that hasbeen brought forward for the entrepreneurs of this country. Imust congratulate the Hon. Minister for the interest he hastaken in the entrepreneurship development of the Sri Lankanentrepreneurs with special mention of the small and mediumenterprise sector. The “Mahinda Chintana” has also givenvery special pride of place to the Sri Lankan businessmenand the industrialists with special notification in regard tothe small and medium enterprise sector.

The Sandhanaya Government fully conscious of the needto develop and uplift this sector has consistently over thelast two budgets made special mention and provision for theupliftment of this sector. The last year saw the formation ofthe Small and Medium Enterprise Development Bank - SMEBank as it is popularly known - with a special feature thatwhile the entrepreneur has to go to the bank for any loans,this bank did not wait for the entrepreneur to come to itsdoorstep but sent its business development officers to thebusiness people to evaluate their businesses, the businesspotential and to offer them help by way of a business plan oreven finances without any need of security. The security, Mr.Deputy Speaker, was only the viability of the project. That isthe type of thing the Sandhanaya Government envisagedand as stated by the previous speakers there may be a fewhitches in the implementation. But by and large I can tellyou having worked in that Ministry for one year, generallythe progress of the SME Bank has been very satisfactory forwhich I must congratulate not only the Hon. Minister butalso his staff in the Ministry who have spared no pains toensure the success of the bank. Unfortunately today we hadto listen to many things not connected to the NationalEnterprise Development Authority. They spoke of the peaceprocess, the cost of living, though there were attempts tojustify it by saying that all these are connected to the NationalEnterprise Development Authority. We heard about theGeneva talks, questions on the Geneva talks. Now on theGeneva talks, I was present at the All Party Conference heldon Monday and the hon. Karu Jayasuriya, deputy leader ofthe United National Party was present and gave his supportto the peace process and did not refer to any of the concerns

raised by one of the previous speakers here. But I am notsurprised because that shows the division within the UnitedNational Party where one section of the party does not knowwhat the other section is doing. Here -

ªÇæ ÍêïÌà¾à ¡ÍÄ ÂÆúÈå ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ÄÊÌ± £Äº´Æ Î¹¾Ç)(The Hon. Hussein Ahamed Bhaila)I am just answering the hon. Member, Mr. Deputy Speaker.Earlier when the Hon. Speaker was in the Chair. Extraneousmatters were raised by the Opposition and this matter wasalso raised. But in any event in deference to you. I willcontinue with my speech on the subject.

Now let us look at the objectives of the National EnterpriseDevelopment Authority. It is to stimulate the growth,expansion and development of Sri Lanka’s economy byencouraging, promoting and facilitating the small andmedium enterprise development within sri Lanka. Is this thesort of thing that the Opposition is opposing? Is theOpposition opposing the development of an Authority tofacilitate the small and medium sector?

The previous speaker spoke about Brandix ApparelLimited and Mahesh Amaleen and Ashroff Omar going toIndia to set up factories. Here we are talking of stimulatingand encouraging the establishments outside Sri Lanka ofenterprises designed to internationalize the domesticenterprises. Are they objecting to our trying to develop othersmall industries, small businessmen going abroad to workfor the country, to get money for the country? Is it that theywant to keep it within a cartel of a few multinationalbusinessmen or a few big businessmen in Sri Lanka at theexpense of small and medium entrepreneurs of this country?This is wht I fail to understand.

We heard people talking about the thosais and the vadaisbeing eaten at Temple Trees. Yes, I am sure they would not behappy because they are the fish and steak eating people whodo not want our small thosai and vadai eating people tocome forward. These are the facts which remain even today.

Clauses 1 to 35 ordered to stand part of the Bill.Schedule, ordered to stand part of the Bill.Enacting Clause and Title ordered to stand part of the Bill.Bill reported with out Amendment.

“the exemplary leadership, commitment and dedication shown bythe relevant District Secretaries, Divisional Secretaries, GramaNiladharies and such other local authorities and agencies in managingthe clearance of thousands of dead bodies, acommodating and facilitat-ing thousands of displaced persons in welfare centers, debris clearingand restoring basic infrastructure to create the access needed to enablerescue and relief operations and the need to take care of state proper-ties, should be recognized in order to understand the gravity of thetasks involved.”

£ Î­´ ¨øÆ¾ ¨åÇ¸Æ §ÂºëÄåºà ÀèÎèª¾à¾å ï¼Æ¨à ¦Íú ºÉóÇ´ºàïÄïÍÄ Ì¿Í¾à ïÉ¾Éå.

“The lack of clarity over the accountability relationships of thecentral, provincial and local governments and financial reporting andoversight arrangements not being well aligned to the needs of a moredevolved system of governance.’’

So this is the reality. You know that. You know the level ofauditing that is going on is the Central Government. There ishardly any auditing in the Provincial Councils and I would

2006 ÄåÚºë 08555556

say that there is no auditing whatsoever in the PradeshiyaSabbhas. So we are creating an environment. hon. Membr,which I know you will appreciate, where we are creating thebackground for corruption. We are looking at so manyantiquated laws. We do not know who is going to enforcethise laws. Consequently I fully agree with the Auditor-General that we are creating an environment in which therecan be a lot of corruption and maladministration and wehave to seriously look at it.

Now what is the burden of this study? What is the burdenof their song?. The burden of their thinking is that Parliamentshould think more of the performance aspect of Government.i think all of us, whichever side of this isle we sit on, are moreand more worried about the handouts we are going to give.We are more and more worried whether these handouts areactually delivered. If you look at some of the interventionsmade in this House, that was also the theme of the song, thatthe Government has allocated these funds but they are notgoing. But now we have to move to a different type of auditwhich is a performance oriented audit. So I am very gratefulto you for raising this matter,Madam. I give you the assuranceon the part of the Government that we will not countenancecorruption and maladministration.

Already I have proposed some measures to the Cabinat sothat those gray areas where people can use their authority tomake money will be reduced. I can give youan assurance thatwe are fully committed and I am willing to believe that youare also committed to create a better environment becausefinally corruption is a tax on the poor man.

(Postage Rs. 2.50) Copies can be obtained by remitting in advance an annual subscription fee to the SUPERINTENDENT,GOVERNMENT PUBLICATION BUREAU, No. 32, Transworks House,Lotus Road, Colombo 1. The fee should reach him on or bvefore November 30 each year.Late application for subscriptions will not be accepted.
